     <p><b>Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</b>, or <b>RPI</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_institute" title="Research institute">research</a> <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Troy,_New_York" title="Troy, New York">Troy, New York</a>. It was founded in 1824 by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer_III" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer III" class="mw-redirect">Stephen Van Rensselaer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amos_Eaton" title="Amos Eaton">Amos Eaton</a> for the &quot;application of science to the common purposes of life&quot; and is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Technological_university" title="Technological university" class="mw-redirect">technological university</a> in the <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world" class="mw-redirect">English-speaking world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Built on a hillside, RPI's 275-acre (111&nbsp;ha) campus overlooks the historic city of Troy and the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> and is a blend of traditional and modern architecture. The institute operates an on?campus <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubator</a> and the 1,250-acre (510&nbsp;ha) <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Technology_Park" title="Rensselaer Technology Park">Rensselaer Technology Park</a>, and is known for its success in the transfer of technology from the laboratory to the marketplace.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is one among a small group of <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Technology_(United_States)#Polytechnic_universities" title="Institute of Technology (United States)">polytechnic universities in the United States</a> which tend to be primarily devoted to the instruction of technical arts and applied sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>RPI's mission has slowly evolved over the years while retaining a focus on the scientific and technological roots upon which it was founded. Over the past century, RPI has grown into a university with five schools: The School of Architecture, The School of Engineering, The School of Humanities, Arts, and Social Sciences, The School of Science, and the <a href="/wiki/Lally_School_of_Management_%26_Technology" title="Lally School of Management &amp; Technology">Lally School of Management &amp; Technology</a>. All together, the university offers around 140&nbsp;degree programs in 60&nbsp;fields leading to bachelor's, master's, and doctoral degrees. RPI consistently ranks in the top 50 among U.S.&nbsp;universities for overall academics and among the top&nbsp;50 worldwide for technology.<sup id="cite_ref-USNEWS_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNEWS-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timestech_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timestech-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Adopted by the Board of Trustees in 1995, RPI's current mission is to &quot;educate the leaders of tomorrow for technologically based careers. We celebrate discovery, and the responsible application of technology, to create knowledge and global prosperity.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The institute attracts students from every state and 92&nbsp;countries. Among class of 2014, 83% were in the top 10% of their high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The acceptance rate was 36.1% in 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-poly_facts_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poly_facts-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> in 2012 it rose to 42.72%.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Rensselaer has been named as a &quot;New <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy</a>&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Kaplan,_Inc." title="Kaplan, Inc.">Kaplan</a>. It remains in the &quot;Top 50 Universities&quot; compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>. Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute also ranks #7 among &quot;Best Engineering Colleges By Salary Potential&quot; in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="History of Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">History of Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1824-1900">1824-1900</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1824-1900">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright" style="width: 250px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 116px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg/114px-StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg" width="114" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg/171px-StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg/228px-StephenVanRensselaerIIIPortrait.jpg 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer_III" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer III" class="mw-redirect">Stephen Van Rensselaer III</a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 122px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Amos_Eaton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Amos_Eaton.jpg/120px-Amos_Eaton.jpg" width="120" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/Amos_Eaton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/Amos_Eaton.jpg 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Amos_Eaton" title="Amos Eaton">Amos Eaton</a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Van_Rensselaer_III" title="Stephen Van Rensselaer III" class="mw-redirect">Stephen Van Rensselaer</a> established the Rensselaer School on November 5, 1824, with a letter to the <a href="/wiki/Rev._Dr._Samuel_Blatchford" title="Rev. Dr. Samuel Blatchford" class="mw-redirect">Rev. Dr. Samuel Blatchford</a>, in which van Rensselaer asked Blatchford to serve as the first president. Within the letter he set down several orders of business. He appointed <a href="/wiki/Amos_Eaton" title="Amos Eaton">Amos Eaton</a> as the school's first senior professor and appointed the first board of trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-historybook_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historybook-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The school opened on Monday, January 3, 1825, at the Old Bank Place, a building at the north end of Troy.<sup id="cite_ref-buildings_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buildings-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Tuition was around $40 per semester.<sup id="cite_ref-historybook_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historybook-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The fact that the school attracted students from as far as Ohio and Pennsylvania is attributed to the reputation of Eaton. Fourteen months of successful trial led to the incorporation of the school on March 21, 1826, by the state of New York. In its early years, the Rensselaer School resembled a graduate school more than it did a college, drawing graduates from many older institutions.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft" style="width: 450px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 234px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rensselaer_School_1824.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rensselaer_School_1824.png/232px-Rensselaer_School_1824.png" width="232" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rensselaer_School_1824.png/348px-Rensselaer_School_1824.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Rensselaer_School_1824.png/464px-Rensselaer_School_1824.png 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Engraving of the original Rensselaer School
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 204px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg/202px-RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg" width="202" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg/303px-RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg/404px-RPI_Engraving_1879.jpg 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Engraving of RPI in 1876
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>During this period, the Rensselaer School, renamed the Rensselaer Institute in 1832, was a small but vital center for technological research. The first civil engineering degrees in the United States were granted by the school in 1835, and many of the best remembered civil engineers of that time graduated from the school. Important visiting scholars included <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Henry" title="Joseph Henry">Joseph Henry</a>, who had previously studied under Amos Eaton, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Davenport_(inventor)" title="Thomas Davenport (inventor)">Thomas Davenport</a>, who sold the world's first working <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motor</a> to the institute.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1847, alumnus <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin_Greene" title="Benjamin Franklin Greene">Benjamin Franklin Greene</a> became the new senior professor. Earlier he had done a thorough study of European technical schools to see how Rensselaer could be improved. In 1850 he reorganized the school into a three-year polytechnic institute with six technical schools.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1861, the name was changed to Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-railroad_guide_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railroad_guide-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> A severe conflagration of May 10, 1862, known as &quot;The Great Fire&quot; destroyed more than 507&nbsp;buildings in Troy and gutted 75 acres (300,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) in the heart of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-great_fire_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-great_fire-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The &quot;Infant School&quot; building that housed the Institute at the time was destroyed in this fire. In response, the campus left the downtown for the hillside which offered potential for expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-great_fire_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-great_fire-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1900-present">1900-present</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1900-present">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="infobox" style="width:200px;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2">Enrollment History:<sup id="cite_ref-railroad_guide_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railroad_guide-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1825: 10 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1850: 53 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1900: 225 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1910: 650 students<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1925: 1,240 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1945: 1,604 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1950: 3,987 students (dormitory construction on &quot;Freshman Hill&quot;)</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>1965: 5,232 students</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>2009: 7,656 students<sup id="cite_ref-quick_facts_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quick_facts-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>RPI enjoyed a period of academic and resource expansion under the leadership of President <a href="/wiki/Palmer_C._Ricketts" title="Palmer C. Ricketts">Palmer Ricketts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Named President in 1901, Ricketts liberalized the curriculum by adding the Department of Arts, Science, and Business Administration, in addition to the Graduate School. He also expanded the university?s resources and developed RPI into a true polytechnic institute by increasing the number of degrees offered from two to twelve; these included electrical engineering, mechanical engineering, biology, chemistry, and physics. During Rickett's tenure, enrollment increased from approximately 200 in 1900 to a high of 1,700 in 1930.<sup id="cite_ref-railroad_guide_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railroad_guide-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another period of expansion occurred following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The &quot;Freshman Hill&quot; residence complex was opened in 1953 followed by the completion of the Commons Dining Hall in 1954, two more halls in 1958, and three more in 1968. In 1961, there was major progress in academics at the institute with the construction of the Gaerttner Linear Accelerator, then the most powerful in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Jonsson-Rowland Science Center. The current Student Union building was opened in 1967.</p> 
     <p>The next three decades brought continued growth with many new buildings (see '<a href="#Campus">Campus'</a> below), and growing ties to industry. The &quot;H-building&quot;, previously used for storage, became the home for the RPI incubator program, the first such program sponsored solely by a university.<sup id="cite_ref-first_incubator_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_incubator-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly after this, RPI decided to invest $3 million in pavement, water and power on around 1,200 acres (490&nbsp;ha) of land it owned 5 miles (8.0&nbsp;km) south of campus to create the <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Technology_Park" title="Rensselaer Technology Park">Rensselaer Technology Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-techpark_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techpark-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1982 the New York State legislature granted RPI $30 million to build the <a href="/wiki/George_M._Low_Center_for_Industrial_Innovation" title="George M. Low Center for Industrial Innovation">George M. Low Center for Industrial Innovation</a>, a center for industry-sponsored research and development.</p> 
     <p>In 1999, RPI gained attention when it was one of the first universities to implement a mandatory <a href="/wiki/Laptop_computer" title="Laptop computer" class="mw-redirect">laptop computer</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> This was also the year of the arrival of President <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Ann_Jackson" title="Shirley Ann Jackson">Shirley Ann Jackson</a>, a former chairperson for the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Regulatory_Commission" title="Nuclear Regulatory Commission">Nuclear Regulatory Commission</a>. She instituted the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute#Rensselaer_Plan" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">The Rensselaer Plan</a>&quot; (discussed below), an ambitious plan to revitalize the institute. Many advances have been made under the plan, and Jackson has enjoyed the ongoing support of the RPI Board of Trustees. However, her leadership style did not sit well with many faculty; on April 26, 2006, RPI faculty voted 149 to 155 in a failed vote of no-confidence in Jackson.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 4, 2008, RPI celebrated the opening of the $220 million <a href="/wiki/Experimental_Media_and_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center">Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center</a>. That same year the national economic downturn resulted in the elimination of 98 positions across the Institute, about five percent of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Campus construction expansion continued, however, with the completion of the $92 million East Campus Athletic Village and opening of the new Blitman Commons residence hall in 2009.</p> 
     <p>With nearly two centuries of history and a high tech future in store, the <i><a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a></i> remarks, ?Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute is simultaneously the oldest technological school in the country and the most modern school of technology in the U.S. It?s like George Jetson meets Archimedes.?<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>RPI's 275-acre (111&nbsp;ha)<sup id="cite_ref-virtual_tour_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virtual_tour-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> landscaped campus sits upon a hill overlooking historic Troy, New York and the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>. The surrounding area is mostly residential neighborhoods, with the city of Troy lying at the base of the hill. The campus is bisected by 15th Street, with most of the athletic and housing facilities to the east, and the academic buildings to the west. An iconic footbridge spans the street, linking the two halves. Much of the campus features a series of <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Revival_style" title="Colonial Revival style" class="mw-redirect">Colonial Revival style</a> structures built in the first three decades of the 20th century. Overall, the campus has enjoyed four periods of expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-buildings_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buildings-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climbing_the_hill.2C_1824.E2.80.931905">Climbing the hill, 1824?1905</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climbing the hill, 1824?1905">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>RPI was originally located in downtown Troy but gradually moved to the hilltop that overlooks the city. Very few buildings from this time period remain.<sup id="cite_ref-buildings_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buildings-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The only building from this time period still located on the RPI campus is the <a href="/wiki/Winslow_Chemical_Laboratory" title="Winslow Chemical Laboratory">Winslow Chemical Laboratory</a>, a building on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. Located at the base of the hill on the western edge of campus, it is currently the home of the Social and Behavioral Research Laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ricketts_Campus.2C_1906.E2.80.931935">Ricketts Campus, 1906?1935</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ricketts Campus, 1906?1935">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RusselSageLabs.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/RusselSageLabs.JPG/220px-RusselSageLabs.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/RusselSageLabs.JPG/330px-RusselSageLabs.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/RusselSageLabs.JPG/440px-RusselSageLabs.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RusselSageLabs.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Russell Sage Laboratory
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>President Palmer Ricketts supervised the construction of the school's &quot;Green Rooftop&quot; Colonial Revival buildings that give much of the campus a distinct architectural style. Buildings constructed during this period include the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Building" title="Carnegie Building">Carnegie Building</a> (1906), Walker Laboratory (1907), Russell Sage Laboratory (1909), Pittsburgh Building (1912), Quadrangle Dormitories (1916?1927), Troy Building (1925), <a href="/wiki/Amos_Eaton_Hall" title="Amos Eaton Hall">Amos Eaton Hall</a> (1928), <a href="/wiki/Greene_Building,_Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Greene Building, Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Greene Building</a> (1931) and Ricketts Building (1935). Also built during this period was &quot;The Approach&quot; (1907), a massive ornate granite staircase found on the west end of campus. Originally linking RPI to the Troy Union Railroad station, it again serves as an important link between the city and the university.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_expansion.2C_1946.E2.80.931960">Post-war expansion, 1946?1960</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-war expansion, 1946?1960">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WestHallRPIPano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/WestHallRPIPano.jpg/220px-WestHallRPIPano.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/WestHallRPIPano.jpg/330px-WestHallRPIPano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/WestHallRPIPano.jpg/440px-WestHallRPIPano.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WestHallRPIPano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/West_Hall_(Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute)" title="West Hall (Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute)">West Hall</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:VorheesComputingCenter.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/VorheesComputingCenter.JPG/220px-VorheesComputingCenter.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/VorheesComputingCenter.JPG/330px-VorheesComputingCenter.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/VorheesComputingCenter.JPG/440px-VorheesComputingCenter.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:VorheesComputingCenter.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Alan_M._Voorhees" title="Alan M. Voorhees" class="mw-redirect">Voorhees</a> Computing Center.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&nbsp;II</a>, the campus again underwent major expansion. Nine dormitories were built at the east edge of campus bordering Burdett Avenue, a location which came to be called &quot;Freshman Hill.&quot; The <a href="/wiki/Houston_Field_House" title="Houston Field House">Houston Field House</a> (1949) was reassembled, after being moved in pieces from its original <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> location. <a href="/wiki/West_Hall_(Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute)" title="West Hall (Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute)">West Hall</a>, which was originally built in 1869 as a hospital, was acquired by the Institute in 1953. The ornate building is an example of <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_(architecture)" title="Second Empire (architecture)" class="mw-redirect">French Second Empire</a> architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> It was listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> in 1973. Another unique building is the Voorhees Computing Center (VCC). Originally built as St.&nbsp;Joseph?s Seminary chapel in 1933, it was once the institute's library, until the completion of the <a href="/wiki/Folsom_Library" title="Folsom Library">Folsom Library</a> in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Interestingly, the new library, built adjacent to the computing center, was designed to match colors with the church, but is very dissimilar architecturally; it is an excellent example of the modern <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalist</a> style ? a style that has invited comparisons with a <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" title="Multi-storey car park">parking garage</a>. The university was unsure of what to do with the church, or whether to keep it at all, but in 1979 the institute decided to preserve it and renovate it into a unique place for computer labs and facilities to support the institute's computing initiatives and today serves as the backbone for the institute's data and telephony infrastructure.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_campus.2C_1961.E2.80.93present">Modern campus, 1961?present</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Modern campus, 1961?present">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:BiotechCenterRPI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BiotechCenterRPI.jpg/220px-BiotechCenterRPI.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BiotechCenterRPI.jpg/330px-BiotechCenterRPI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/BiotechCenterRPI.jpg/440px-BiotechCenterRPI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:BiotechCenterRPI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biotechnology_and_Interdisciplinary_Studies" title="Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies">Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:EMPACTwilight.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/EMPACTwilight.JPG/220px-EMPACTwilight.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/EMPACTwilight.JPG/330px-EMPACTwilight.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/EMPACTwilight.JPG/440px-EMPACTwilight.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:EMPACTwilight.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Experimental_Media_and_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center">EMPAC</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The modern campus features the Jonsson-Rowland Science Center (J-ROWL) (1961), Materials Research Center (MRC) (1965), Rensselaer Union (1967), Cogswell Laboratory (1971), Darrin Communications Center (DCC) (1973), <a href="/wiki/Jonsson_Engineering_Center" title="Jonsson Engineering Center">Jonsson Engineering Center</a> (JEC) (1977), <a href="/wiki/Low_Center_for_Industrial_Innovation" title="Low Center for Industrial Innovation" class="mw-redirect">Low Center for Industrial Innovation</a> (CII) (1987), a public school building which was converted into Academy Hall (1990), and the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biotechnology_and_Interdisciplinary_Studies" title="Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies">Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies</a> (2004).<sup id="cite_ref-buildings_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buildings-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Although rarely used by students, tunnels connect the Low Center, DCC, JEC and Science Center. A tenth dormitory named Barton Hall was added to Freshman Hill in August 2000, featuring the largest rooms available for freshmen.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On October 4, 2008, the university celebrated the grand opening of the <a href="/wiki/Experimental_Media_and_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center">Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center</a> (EMPAC) situated on the west edge of campus.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The building was constructed on the precipice of the hill, with the main entrance on top. Upon entering, elevated walkways lead into a 1,200 seat concert hall. Most of the building is encased in a glass exoskeleton, with an atrium-like space between it and the &quot;inner building&quot;. Adjacent to and underneath the main auditorium there is a 400-seat theater, offices, and three studios with 40-foot (12&nbsp;m) to 60-foot (18&nbsp;m) ceilings.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In October 2007, tentative plans were announced by President Jackson for a major addition to the Jonsson-Rowland Science Center, which would add 100,000 square feet (9,300&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) to 120,000 square feet (11,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of lab space.<sup id="cite_ref-Shirley_Speech_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shirley_Speech-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Design mock-ups showed a new adjacent building built next to the Science Center, with a glass-enclosed atrium spanning the space between the old building and the new.<sup id="cite_ref-Shirley_Speech_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shirley_Speech-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The plans were further elaborated on by Jackson at the 2008 Town Meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-spring_meeting_2008_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spring_meeting_2008-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> It was announced that under the plan the <a href="/wiki/Hirsch_Observatory" title="Hirsch Observatory">Hirsch Observatory</a> would be renovated as well.<sup id="cite_ref-polynewscience_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polynewscience-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Vice President Claude Rounds said the budget had not been worked out in full but the project should cost somewhere between $70 to $75 million.<sup id="cite_ref-polynewscience_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polynewscience-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2008, no further official announcements on the project have been made and the status of the project is unknown.</p> 
     <p>In 2008, RPI announced the purchase of the former Rensselaer <a href="/wiki/Best_Western" title="Best Western">Best Western</a> Inn, located at the base of the hill, along with plans to transform it into a new residence hall. After extensive renovations, the residence hall was dedicated on May 15, 2009, as the Howard N. Blitman, P.E. ?50 Residence Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-bestwestern_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bestwestern-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> It houses about 300 students in 148&nbsp;rooms and includes a fitness center, dining hall, and conference area.<sup id="cite_ref-bestwestern_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bestwestern-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The new residence hall is part of a growing initiative to involve students in the Troy community and help revitalize the downtown. RPI owns and operates three office buildings in downtown Troy, the Rice and Heley buildings and the historic <a href="/wiki/W._%26_L.E._Gurley_Building" title="W. &amp; L.E. Gurley Building" class="mw-redirect">W. &amp; L.E. Gurley Building</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> RPI also owns the <a href="/wiki/Proctor%27s_Theater_(Troy,_New_York)" title="Proctor's Theater (Troy, New York)">Proctor's Theater</a> building in Troy which was purchased in 2004, with the intention of converting it into office space.<sup id="cite_ref-RPI_purchase_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPI_purchase-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to the historic nature of the building, there was resistance by the Troy community and RPI has not done any redevelopment. Advocates are hoping to restore the building back to its original use.<sup id="cite_ref-Liz_Young_TU_blog_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liz_Young_TU_blog-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gutting_proposal_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gutting_proposal-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_campuses">Other campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_at_Hartford" title="Rensselaer at Hartford">Rensselaer at Hartford</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Institute runs a 15-acre (6.1&nbsp;ha) campus in <a href="/wiki/Hartford,_Connecticut" title="Hartford, Connecticut">Hartford, Connecticut</a>, and a distance learning center in <a href="/wiki/Groton,_Connecticut" title="Groton, Connecticut">Groton, Connecticut</a>. These centers are used by graduates and working professionals and are managed by the Hartford branch of RPI, <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_at_Hartford" title="Rensselaer at Hartford">Rensselaer at Hartford</a>. At Hartford, graduate degrees are offered in <a href="/wiki/Business_administration" title="Business administration">business administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_engineering" title="Computer engineering">computer and systems engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, engineering science, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>. There are also a number of certificate programs and skills training programs for working professionals.</p> 
     <p>RPI also has a location in <a href="/wiki/Malta,_New_York" title="Malta, New York">Malta, New York</a>, for graduates of the Navy Nuclear Power Training School (NNPTS) who work at the <a href="/wiki/Knolls_Atomic_Power_Laboratory" title="Knolls Atomic Power Laboratory">Knolls Atomic Power Laboratory</a>'s (KAPL) <a href="/wiki/Kesselring" title="Kesselring">Kesselring</a> Site Operation in nearby <a href="/wiki/West_Milton,_New_York" title="West Milton, New York">West Milton</a>. Faculty from the Troy campus provide the teaching. Students enter with one year's worth of coursework and in two to three years graduate with a bachelor's degree in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_engineering" title="Nuclear engineering">nuclear engineering</a>, engineering physics or engineering science.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIAcademyHall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RPIAcademyHall.JPG/220px-RPIAcademyHall.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RPIAcademyHall.JPG/330px-RPIAcademyHall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/RPIAcademyHall.JPG/440px-RPIAcademyHall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIAcademyHall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Academy Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute has five schools: the School of Architecture, the School of Engineering, the School of Humanities, Arts, and Social Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/Lally_School_of_Management_%26_Technology" title="Lally School of Management &amp; Technology">Lally School of Management &amp; Technology</a>, and the School of Science. The School of Engineering is the largest by enrollment, followed by the School of Science, the School of Management, the School of Humanities, Arts, and Social Sciences, and the School of Architecture. There also exists an interdisciplinary program in <a href="/wiki/Information_Technology" title="Information Technology" class="mw-redirect">Information Technology</a> that began in the late 1990s, programs in prehealth and prelaw, <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Officers%27_Training_Corps" title="Reserve Officers' Training Corps">Reserve Officers' Training Corps</a> (ROTC) for students desiring commissions as officers in the armed forces, a program in <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_education" title="Cooperative education">cooperative education</a> (Co-Op), and domestic and international exchange programs. All together, the university offers around 140 degree programs in nearly 60 fields that lead to bachelor's, master's, and doctoral degrees. In addition to traditional majors, RPI has around a dozen special interdisciplinary programs, such as Games and Simulation Arts and Sciences (GSAS), Design, Innovation, and Society (DIS), Minds &amp; Machines, and Product Design and Innovation (PDI).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> RPI is a technology-oriented university; all buildings and residence hall rooms have hard-wired high speed internet access, most of the campus buildings have wireless, and all incoming freshmen have been required to have a laptop computer since 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> ranked RPI first in terms of wireless as the &quot;most connected campus&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Nationally, RPI is a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Independent_Colleges_and_Universities" title="National Association of Independent Colleges and Universities">National Association of Independent Colleges and Universities</a> (NAICU) and the NAICU's <a href="/wiki/University_and_College_Accountability_Network" title="University and College Accountability Network">University and College Accountability Network</a> (U-CAN).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rensselaer_Plan">Rensselaer Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rensselaer Plan">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIPano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RPIPano.jpg/350px-RPIPano.jpg" width="350" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RPIPano.jpg/525px-RPIPano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/RPIPano.jpg/700px-RPIPano.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIPano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View of RPI from 
        <a href="/wiki/Central_Troy_Historic_District" title="Central Troy Historic District">downtown Troy</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With the arrival of the current president, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Ann_Jackson" title="Shirley Ann Jackson">Shirley Ann Jackson</a>, came the &quot;Rensselaer Plan&quot; announced in 1999. Its goal is to achieve greater prominence for RPI as a technological research university.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Various aspects of the plan include bringing in a larger <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student" class="mw-redirect">graduate student</a> population and new research faculty, and increasing participation in undergraduate research, international exchange programs, and &quot;living and learning communities&quot;. Financially speaking, the plan uses half its money for <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a>, a quarter for scholarships, and a quarter for campus platforms, such as athletic facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> So far, there have been a number of changes under the plan: new infrastructure such as the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biotechnology_and_Interdisciplinary_Studies" title="Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies">Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computational_Center_for_Nanotechnology_Innovations" title="Computational Center for Nanotechnology Innovations">Computational Center for Nanotechnology Innovations</a> (CCNI) was built to support new programs, and application numbers have increased.<sup id="cite_ref-accomplished_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accomplished-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> In fact, in the three years between 2005 and 2008 application numbers doubled from 5,500 to 11,000.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Jared_Cohon" title="Jared Cohon">Jared Cohon</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> ?Change at Rensselaer in the last five years has occurred with a scope and swiftness that may be without precedent in the recent history of American higher education.?<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Although the number of doctoral students has increased,<sup id="cite_ref-accomplished_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accomplished-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> the plan has not increased the overall number of graduate students. The number of graduates on the Troy campus has dropped from a high of 2,617 in 1999 to 1,228 in 2007, a decrease of more than 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> These pages show a decrease from 1,839 in 1999 to 1,228 in 2007, a decrease of 36% (Hartford students were not included in the 1999 figure).</p> 
     <p>The ability to attract greater research funds is needed to meet the goals of the plan, and the university has set a goal of $100&nbsp;million annually. In 2006, research expenditures reached $90&nbsp;million per annum. The university recognizes the relatively small size of its <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a> compared to its competition (cf. Case Western Reserve U., University of Rochester, etc.). To help raise money the university mounted a $1&nbsp;billion capital campaign, of which the public phase began in September 2004 and was expected to finish by 2008. In 2001, a major milestone of the campaign was the pledging of an unrestricted gift of $360&nbsp;million by an anonymous donor, believed to be the largest such gift to a U.S.&nbsp;university at the time. The university had been a relative stranger to such generosity as the prior largest single gift was $15&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> By September 2006, the $1 billion goal has been exceeded much in part to an in-kind contribution of software commercially-valued at $513.95&nbsp;million by the Partners for the Advancement of Collaborative Engineering Education (PACE). In light of this, the board of trustees announced a new goal of $1.4 billion by June 30, 2009. The new goal was met by October 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The number of faculty has been steadily growing since the implementation of the Rensselaer Plan in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-accomplished_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accomplished-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Among them are members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academies" title="National Academies" class="mw-redirect">National Academies</a>, a Nobel laureate, and 40 NSF Faculty Early Career Development Award winners.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006 there are 400 full-time and 81 part-time faculty members, yielding a student-faculty ratio of 14:1.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Well-known faculty members include:</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg/220px-TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg/330px-TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg/440px-TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TroyBuildingPanorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Troy Building, which houses the president's office
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Selmer_Bringsjord" title="Selmer Bringsjord">Selmer Bringsjord</a> - <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> researcher</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Dordick" title="Jonathan Dordick">Jonathan Dordick</a> - leader of a group doing <a href="/wiki/Biochemical_engineering" title="Biochemical engineering">biochemical engineering</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Ivar_Giaever" title="Ivar Giaever">Ivar Giaever</a> ('64) - Nobel laureate 1973 and physics professor emeritus</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/James_Hendler" title="James Hendler">James Hendler</a> - <a href="/wiki/Computer_scientist" title="Computer scientist">computer scientist</a> and author</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/David_Musser" title="David Musser">David Musser</a> - one of the primary persons behind the <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> <a href="/wiki/Standard_Template_Library" title="Standard Template Library">Standard Template Library</a><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Leik_Myrabo" title="Leik Myrabo">Leik Myrabo</a> - known for designing and testing laser &quot;lightcraft&quot; propulsion systems</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Pauline_Oliveros" title="Pauline Oliveros">Pauline Oliveros</a> - musician and composer of electronic art music</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Resnick" title="Robert Resnick">Robert Resnick</a> - textbook author and physics professor emeritus</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Sal_Restivo" title="Sal Restivo">Sal Restivo</a> - pioneering researcher in the ethnography of science and social studies of mathematics; founding member and former president of the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_Social_Studies_of_Science" title="Society for Social Studies of Science">Society for Social Studies of Science</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Neil_Rolnick" title="Neil Rolnick">Neil Rolnick</a> - former head of the Arts Department, and founder of iEAR studios</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Shur" title="Michael Shur">Michael Shur</a>- well-published <a href="/wiki/Solid_state_(electronics)" title="Solid state (electronics)" class="mw-redirect">solid state electronics</a> researcher</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Boleslaw_Szymanski" title="Boleslaw Szymanski">Boleslaw Szymanski</a> - <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Fellow" title="IEEE Fellow">IEEE Fellow</a> and a foreign member of <a href="/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Polish Academy of Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Igor_Vamos" title="Igor Vamos">Igor Vamos</a> - multimedia artist and leading member of <a href="/wiki/Culture_jamming" title="Culture jamming">culture jamming</a> duo <a href="/wiki/The_Yes_Men" title="The Yes Men">The Yes Men</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Langdon_Winner" title="Langdon Winner">Langdon Winner</a> - leading political philosopher of technology</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Xi-Cheng_Zhang" title="Xi-Cheng Zhang">Xi-Cheng Zhang</a> - head of the Center for <a href="/wiki/Terahertz_radiation" title="Terahertz radiation">Terahertz</a> Research</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>RPI ranks among the top 50 national universities in the United States according to <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-USNEWS_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNEWS-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The same source ranks RPI 24th for &quot;Best Value&quot; in undergraduate education.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, the School of Engineering was ranked 16th in the nation for undergraduates, and 34th in the nation for graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-RPI_rankings_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPI_rankings-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Four of the graduate engineering programs are ranked in the top 20 (electrical engineering, materials science and engineering, industrial engineering and mechanical engineering), seven of 11 are ranked in the top 25, and all are ranked in the top 40 in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006 <i>U.S. News</i> put the graduate applied mathematics program at 20th.<sup id="cite_ref-rankings_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankings-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>/<a href="/wiki/Kaplan,_Inc." title="Kaplan, Inc.">Kaplan</a> 2007 Educational College Guide named Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute one of the 25 &quot;New Ivies&quot;, a group of 25 schools described as providing an education equivalent to schools in the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Lally School of Management and Technology?s entrepreneurship programs ranked 21st in the USA, and its technological entrepreneurship program was ranked sixth by <i><a href="/wiki/Entrepreneur_Magazine" title="Entrepreneur Magazine" class="mw-redirect">Entrepreneur</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-rankings_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankings-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Lally School's corporate strategy program was ranked eleventh in the nation by <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-lally_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lally-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The electronic arts program is one of the highest ranked departments at RPI. For four years in a row, 2003, 2004, 2005 and 2006, <i>U.S. News</i> ranked the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.arts.rpi.edu/">iEAR program</a> 8th in the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-rankings_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankings-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Master of Fine Arts in multimedia/visual communications program was ranked 6th in 2008 and 2009 by <i>U.S. News</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2008, a new ranking called <a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#Forbes_College_rankings" title="College and university rankings">America's Best Colleges</a> released by Forbes.com placed RPI at 49,<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and then at 42 a year later in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2009_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2009-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, <i>Forbes</i> and Payscale.com reported that among U.S.&nbsp;colleges, RPI had the 9th highest average starting salary and 13th highest average mid-career salary for graduates, based on actual earnings information.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2008 <a href="/wiki/THES_-_QS_World_University_Rankings" title="THES - QS World University Rankings" class="mw-redirect">THES - QS World University Rankings</a> ranks RPI at 174 among the top 200 universities worldwide for overall academics,<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighered_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighered-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> and number 50 among the top 50 universities for technology.<sup id="cite_ref-timestech_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timestech-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2010-2011 <i>Times Higher Education</i> rankings show RPI moving up to 104 among the world's top 200 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The Global University Ranking, which utilizes a combination of major international ranking systems, ranked RPI in the range 74-77 in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, RPI was ranked as the 4th best engineering school in the world by <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Research and development">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:LowCenterRPI.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/LowCenterRPI.JPG/220px-LowCenterRPI.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/LowCenterRPI.JPG/330px-LowCenterRPI.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/LowCenterRPI.JPG/440px-LowCenterRPI.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:LowCenterRPI.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Low_Center_for_Industrial_Innovation" title="Low Center for Industrial Innovation" class="mw-redirect">Low Center for Industrial Innovation</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>RPI has established six areas of research as institute priorities: <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy and the environment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_Technology" title="Information Technology" class="mw-redirect">computation and information technology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Media_studies" title="Media studies">media and the arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Advances in these fields have the potential to effect dramatic transformations in 21st century society.</p> 
     <p>Some notable research centers operated by RPI are the Terahertz Research Center, <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Biotechnology_and_Interdisciplinary_Studies" title="Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies">Center for Biotechnology and Interdisciplinary Studies</a>, Rensselaer Nanotechnology Center, New York State Center for Polymer Synthesis, Darrin Fresh Water Institute, Center for Automation Technologies and Systems, and the Lighting Research Center.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The Lighting Research Center (LRC) is the leading university-based research center devoted to lighting, offering the world's only master's degree in lighting. Since 1988, it has built an international reputation as a reliable source for objective information about lighting technologies, applications, and products. The LRC provides training programs for government agencies, utilities, contractors, lighting designers, and other lighting professionals.</p> 
     <p>RPI conducts nuclear research at the 60MeV Gaerttner <a href="/wiki/Linear_particle_accelerator" title="Linear particle accelerator">Linear Accelerator</a> (LINAC) Laboratory. The LINAC is used primarily for the testing of materials, but there is also ongoing research in <a href="/wiki/Neutron_generator" title="Neutron generator">neutron generation</a> and other technologies. The lab made the news with discoveries regarding <a href="/wiki/Bubble_fusion" title="Bubble fusion">bubble fusion</a><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and portable <a href="/wiki/Pyroelectric_fusion" title="Pyroelectric fusion">pyroelectric fusion</a> devices.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Other important research facilities include the geotechnical centrifuge, used for civil engineering simulations, and RPI's array of six subsonic, supersonic and hypersonic <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In May 2006, RPI announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> and the state of New York to create the <a href="/wiki/Computational_Center_for_Nanotechnology_Innovations" title="Computational Center for Nanotechnology Innovations">Computational Center for Nanotechnology Innovations</a>, a supercomputing center to be used for <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a> research. In June 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Gene" title="Blue Gene">Blue Gene</a> system at the center was the 76th most powerful supercomputer in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2013, IBM said that RPI will receive a successor version of its <a href="/wiki/Watson_(computer)" title="Watson (computer)">Watson</a> computer. It will be housed at the Institute's technology park and be available to researchers and students.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>RPI has the United States' first on-campus business incubator,<sup id="cite_ref-first_incubator_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_incubator-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> which has helped start over 180 companies in its lifetime, with a survival rate of about 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> One of the largest companies to have originated in the incubator is <a href="/wiki/MapInfo" title="MapInfo">MapInfo</a>, a major publisher of mapping and geographic information systems software. Others incubator success stories include <a href="/wiki/Vicarious_Visions" title="Vicarious Visions">Vicarious Visions</a>, a well known maker of video games, and CORESense,&nbsp;Inc., a leading provider of multi-channel retail software. RPI operates the <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Technology_Park" title="Rensselaer Technology Park">Rensselaer Technology Park</a>, which is home to over 50 technologically oriented companies. The 1,250-acre (510&nbsp;ha) park is about 5 miles (8.0&nbsp;km) south of the campus along the Hudson River.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Park tenants collaborate with faculty and students on research projects and hire students for internships, co-ops and employment.</p> 
     <p>In conjunction with the incubator, Professor Gina O'Connor launched the Radical Innovation Project (RIP) at RPI, which is a project to create innovative <a href="/wiki/New_product_development" title="New product development">new products</a> out of new technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The approach is to start with a new technology, and then find radical innovations and product concepts, rather than the usual approach which starts with a problem and then looks for a technological solution.<sup id="cite_ref-Griffin_2009_225_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin_2009_225-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> All projects originate out of <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> projects. The study of those projects is expected to provide insight on how to manage the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Fuzzy_front_end" title="Fuzzy front end" class="mw-redirect">fuzzy front end</a>&quot;: the earliest, most unclear stage of product innovation when innovators do not know what will eventually be the product. It was found that early product research generally does not employ a highly structured process as in the case of managing incremental NPD processes, but they follow logical processes. Such ultra-early stage are more exploratory and less customer driven. Possibly prototypes are developed at an early stage, preceding opportunity analysis, market research, and financial analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-Griffin_2009_225_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin_2009_225-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The Radical Innovation Project approach has been the subject of several research publications.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Students">Students</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Students">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIQuad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RPIQuad.jpg/300px-RPIQuad.jpg" width="300" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RPIQuad.jpg/450px-RPIQuad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/RPIQuad.jpg/600px-RPIQuad.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIQuad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> RPI's &quot;Quad&quot; dormitory on the central campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the 2008?2009 academic year, RPI's enrollment included 5,534 resident undergraduate, 1,055 resident graduate, 722 graduate students on the Hartford campus, and 71 distance learning graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The institute attracts students from every state and 92 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the class of 2014, 80% were in the top 10% of their high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The average high school GPA of the class of 2013 was a 3.9 and the average SAT score was 1420.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The acceptance rate dropped between 2005?11 and in 2011 was 37.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-poly_facts_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poly_facts-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The yield rate (percentage of admitted students who attend) was 27.3% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Around 17% of students received the RPI medal/scholarship in high school, which is a merit scholarship of $15,000 a year.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Altogether about 90% of students receive either need-based or merit-based financial aid.<sup id="cite_ref-financial_aid_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financial_aid-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_ratio">Gender ratio</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Gender ratio">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Since becoming coeducational in 1942, RPI has struggled to attract a gender-balanced applicant pool. In 1966, the male-to-female ratio was 19:1, in the 1980s it reached as high as 8:1, and in the early 1990s the ratio was around 5:1. In 2009, RPI had a ratio of 2.5:1 (72% male / 28% female),<sup id="cite_ref-Common_Data_Set_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Common_Data_Set-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Both the class of 2011 and the class of 2012 have a ratio of about 2.3:1, or about 30% female.<sup id="cite_ref-poly_facts_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poly_facts-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As is common among universities, the male-to-female ratio does vary between schools and individual majors. One of the stated goals of the Rensselaer Plan is to &quot;reflect the diversity of the global community&quot; in the student body, which includes encouraging more women to enroll.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPI_Engineers.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/RPI_Engineers.svg/150px-RPI_Engineers.svg.png" width="150" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/RPI_Engineers.svg/225px-RPI_Engineers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/RPI_Engineers.svg/300px-RPI_Engineers.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPI_Engineers.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> RPI Athletics logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/RPI_Engineers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="RPI Engineers men's ice hockey">RPI Engineers men's ice hockey</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/RPI_Engineers_women%27s_ice_hockey" title="RPI Engineers women's ice hockey">RPI Engineers women's ice hockey</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <b>RPI Engineers</b> are the athletic teams for the university. RPI currently sponsors 23&nbsp;sports, 21 of which compete at the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division&nbsp;III</a> level in the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_League" title="Liberty League">Liberty League</a>; men's and women's ice hockey compete at the <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division&nbsp;I</a> level in <a href="/wiki/ECAC_Hockey" title="ECAC Hockey">ECAC Hockey</a>. The official nickname of some of the school's Division&nbsp;III teams was changed in 1995 from the Engineers to the Red Hawks. However, the hockey, football, cross-country, tennis and track and field teams all chose to retain the Engineers name. The Red Hawks name was, at the time, very unpopular among the student body; a Red Hawk mascot was frequently taunted with thrown concessions and chants of &quot;kill the chicken!&quot;. The nickname has since been changed back to Engineers. In contrast, the official ice hockey mascot, known as The Puckman, has always been very popular. The Puckman is an anthropomorphic hockey puck with an engineer's helmet.</p> 
     <p>During the 1970s and 1980s, one RPI cheer was:</p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <i>E to the x, dy/dx, E to the x, dx</i>
      </dd> 
      <dd>
       <i>Cosine, secant, tangent, sine</i>
      </dd> 
      <dd>
       <i>3.14159</i>
      </dd> 
      <dd>
       <i>Square root, cube root, log of pi</i>
      </dd> 
      <dd>
       <i>Disintegrate them, RPI!</i>
       <sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
       <sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey_.28men.27s.29">Ice hockey (men's)</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ice hockey (men's)">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPI_Puckman_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/RPI_Puckman_logo.png/150px-RPI_Puckman_logo.png" width="150" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/RPI_Puckman_logo.png/225px-RPI_Puckman_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2b/RPI_Puckman_logo.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPI_Puckman_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Puckman Mascot.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>RPI has a competitive Division&nbsp;I <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team, the Engineers, who won <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> national titles in 1954 and 1985. Depending on how the rules are interpreted, the RPI men's ice hockey team may have the longest winning streak on record for a Division&nbsp;I team; in the 1984-85 season it was undefeated for 30&nbsp;games, but one game was against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a>, a non-NCAA team. Continuing into the 1985-86 season, RPI continued undefeated over 38&nbsp;games, including two wins over Toronto.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adam_Oates" title="Adam Oates">Adam Oates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daren_Puppa" title="Daren Puppa">Daren Puppa</a>, two players during that time, both went on to become stars in the NHL. <a href="/wiki/Joe_Juneau" title="Joe Juneau" class="mw-redirect">Joe Juneau</a>, who played from 1987 to 1991, and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Pothier" title="Brian Pothier">Brian Pothier</a>, who played from 1996?2000, also spent many years in the NHL. <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Townshend" title="Graeme Townshend">Graeme Townshend</a>, who also played in the late 1980s, had a brief NHL career. He is the first person of <a href="/wiki/Jamaican" title="Jamaican" class="mw-redirect">Jamaican</a> ancestry to play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>.</p> 
     <p>The ice hockey team plays a significant role in the campus's culture, drawing thousands of fans each week to the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Field_House" title="Houston Field House">Houston Field House</a> during the season.
