The team's popularity even sparked the tradition of the hockey line, where students lined up for season tickets months in advance of the on-sale date. Today, the line generally begins a week or more before ticket sales.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Another tradition since 1978 has been the &quot;Big Red Freakout!&quot; game held close to the first weekend of February. Fans usually dress in the schools colors red and white, and gifts such as T-shirts are distributed en masse. In ice hockey, the RPI's biggest rival has always been the upstate engineering school <a href="/wiki/Clarkson_University" title="Clarkson University">Clarkson University</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey_.28women.27s.29">Ice hockey (women's)</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ice hockey (women's)">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The women's ice hockey team moved to the NCAA Division I level in 2005. During the 2008-09 season the team set the record for most wins in one season (19-14-4). On February 28, 2010, Rensselaer made NCAA history. The Engineers beat Quinnipiac, 2-1, but it took five overtimes. It is now the longest college hockey game in NCAA history. Senior defenseman Laura Gersten had the game-winning goal. She registered it at 4:32 of the fifth overtime session to not only clinch the win, but the series victory.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lacrosse_.28men.27s.29">Lacrosse (men's)</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lacrosse (men's)">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> team won the <a href="/wiki/Wingate_Memorial_Trophy" title="Wingate Memorial Trophy">national championship</a> in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> The lacrosse team also represented the United States in the <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse_at_the_1948_Summer_Olympics" title="Lacrosse at the 1948 Summer Olympics">1948 Olympics</a> in London. <a href="/wiki/Ned_Harkness" title="Ned Harkness">Ned Harkness</a> coached the lacrosse and ice hockey teams, winning national championships in both sports.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Red Hawk baseball squad is perennially atop the Liberty League standings, and has seen 8 players move on to the professional ranks, including 4 players selected in the MLB draft. The team is coached by the ex?New York Yankee Karl Steffen (Ithaca '78) with Steve &quot;Smoke&quot; Allard (Massachusetts '87) as associate head coach and Kyle Meyer (Marist '09) as assistant coach. The Red Hawks play their home games at the historic Robison Field.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_football">American football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: American football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Since 1903, RPI and nearby Union College have been rivals in football, making it the oldest such rivalry in the state. The teams play for the <a href="/wiki/Dutchman%27s_Shoes" title="Dutchman's Shoes">Dutchman's Shoes</a>. RPI Football had their most successful season in 2003, when they finished 11-2 and lost to St. Johns (Minn.) in the NCAA Division III semi final game.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletic_facilities">Athletic facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Athletic facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg/220px-RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg/330px-RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg/440px-RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIHoustonFieldHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Houston Field House
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIAthleticVillage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/RPIAthleticVillage.jpg/300px-RPIAthleticVillage.jpg" width="300" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/RPIAthleticVillage.jpg/450px-RPIAthleticVillage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/RPIAthleticVillage.jpg/600px-RPIAthleticVillage.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIAthleticVillage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> East Campus Athletic Village, under construction
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Houston_Field_House" title="Houston Field House">Houston Field House</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Houston Field House is a 4,780?seat multi-purpose arena located on the RPI campus. It opened in 1949 and is home to the RPI Engineers men's and women's ice hockey teams. The Field House was renovated starting in 2007 as part of the major campus improvement project to build the East Campus Athletic Village. The renovations included locker rooms upgrades, addition of a new weight room, and a new special reception room dedicated to Ned Harkness.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, as part of the renovations through a government grant, solar panels were installed on the roof to supply power to the building.</p> 
     <p>As part of the Rensselaer Plan, the Institute recently completed a major project to improve its athletic facilities with the East Campus Athletic Village. The plan included construction of a new and much larger 4,842?seat football stadium, a basketball arena with seating for 1,200, a new 50-meter pool, an indoor track and field complex, new tennis courts, new weight rooms and a new sports medicine center.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The Institute broke ground on August 26, 2007, and construction of the first phase is expected to last two years.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The estimated cost of the project is $78 million for phase one and $35?$45 million for phase two.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Since the completion of the new stadium, the bleachers on the Class of '86 football field on the central campus have been removed and the field has become an open space. In the future the new space could be used for expansions of the academic buildings, but for now members of the campus planning team foresee a &quot;historic landscape with different paths and access ways for students and vehicles alike&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIStudentUnion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RPIStudentUnion.jpg/300px-RPIStudentUnion.jpg" width="300" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RPIStudentUnion.jpg/450px-RPIStudentUnion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/RPIStudentUnion.jpg/600px-RPIStudentUnion.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIStudentUnion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Student Union.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The students of RPI have created and participate in a variety of student-run clubs and organizations funded by the Student Union. The Union is unusual in that it is entirely student-run and its operations are paid for by activity fees. About 170 of these organizations are funded by the Student Union, while another thirty, which consist mostly of political and religious organizations, are self-supporting.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006 the <i>Princeton Review</i> ranked RPI second for &quot;more to do on campus.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Phalanx is RPI's Senior Honor Society.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> It was founded in 1912, when Edward Dion and the Student Council organized a society to recognize those RPI students who had distinguished themselves among their peers in the areas of leadership, service and devotion to the <i>alma mater</i>. It is a fellowship of the most active in student activities and has inducted more than 1,300 members since its founding.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Greek organizations are popular with about 30 social fraternities and five sororities. There are two co?ed fraternities, <a href="/wiki/Epsilon_Iota" title="Epsilon Iota" class="mw-redirect">Psi Upsilon</a>, a social fraternity, while the other, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Service_fraternities_and_sororities" title="Service fraternities and sororities">service fraternity</a>. As such, about a third of men are in fraternities and about a fifth of women are in sororities. (See the <a href="/wiki/List_of_RPI_fraternities_and_sororities" title="List of RPI fraternities and sororities">List of RPI fraternities and sororities</a>.)</p> 
     <p>RPI has around twenty intramural sports organizations, many of which are broken down into different divisions based on level of play. Greek organizations compete in them as well as independent athletes. There are also thirty-nine club sports.</p> 
     <p>Given the university's proximity to the Berkshires, Green Mountains and Adirondacks, the Ski Club and the Outing Club are some of the largest groups on campus. The Ski Club offers weekly trips to local ski areas during the winter months,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> while the Outing Club offers trips on a weekly basis for a variety of activities.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Rensselaer_Polytechnic" title="The Rensselaer Polytechnic">The Rensselaer Polytechnic</a></i> is the student-run weekly newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Poly</i> prints about 7,000 copies each week and distributes them around campus. Although it is the Union club with the largest budget, <i>The Poly</i> receives no subsidy from the Union, and obtains all funding through the sale of advertisements. There is also a popular student-run magazine called <i>Statler &amp; Waldorf</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-SW_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SW-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>RPI has an improvisational comedy group, Sheer Idiocy, which performs several shows a semester.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> There are also several music groups ranging from <i><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a></i> groups such as the Rensselyrics, the Rusty Pipes, Partial Credit and Duly Noted,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> to several instrumental groups such as the Orchestra, the Jazz Band and a classical choral group, the Rensselaer Concert Choir.</p> 
     <p>Another notable organization on campus is <a href="/wiki/WRPI" title="WRPI">WRPI</a>, the campus radio station. WRPI differs from most <a href="/wiki/College_radio" title="College radio" class="mw-redirect">college radio</a> in that it serves a 75-mile (121&nbsp;km) radius<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> including the greater <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a> area. With 10&nbsp;kW of broadcasting power, WRPI maintains a stronger signal than nearly all college radio stations and some commercial stations. WRPI currently broadcasts on 91.5&nbsp;FM in the Albany area.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:RPIPlayhouse2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/RPIPlayhouse2.jpg/220px-RPIPlayhouse2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/RPIPlayhouse2.jpg/330px-RPIPlayhouse2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/RPIPlayhouse2.jpg/440px-RPIPlayhouse2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:RPIPlayhouse2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The RPI Playhouse.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The RPI Players is an on?campus theater group that was formed in 1929. The Players resided in the Old Gym until 1965 when they moved to their present location at the 15th&nbsp;Street Lounge. This distinctive red shingled building had been a USO hall for the U.S.&nbsp;Army before being purchased by RPI. The Players have staged over 275 productions in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RPI_songs">RPI songs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: RPI songs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/RPI_songs" title="RPI songs" class="mw-redirect">RPI songs</a>
     </div> 
     <p>There are a number of songs commonly played and sung at RPI events.<sup id="cite_ref-songs_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-songs-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stutt_songs_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stutt_songs-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable among them are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><i>The Alma Mater (Here's to Old RPI)</i> - sung at formal events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, also played and sung by the <a href="/wiki/Pep_band" title="Pep band">Pep Band</a> at hockey and football games. It was published in the first book of <i>Songs of Rensselaer</i> printed in 1913.</li> 
      <li><i>Hail, Dear Old Rensselaer</i> - used to be the <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> during the 1960s. It is still played today by the Pep Band at athletic events.</li> 
      <li><i>All We've Learned at Rensselaer</i> - sung at the RPI commencement ceremonies by the Rensselyrics. Although the Rensselyrics are an <i><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a></i> group, this song is accompanied by piano. Each verse or section has a different musical style, several of which are closely based on <a href="/wiki/Billy_Joel" title="Billy Joel">Billy Joel</a> songs or other popular songs.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Year_Experience_and_CLASS_programs">First Year Experience and CLASS programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: First Year Experience and CLASS programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Another notable aspect of student life at RPI is the &quot;First-Year Experience&quot; (FYE) program. Freshman begin their stay at RPI with a week called &quot;Navigating Rensselaer and Beyond&quot; or NRB week. The Office of the First-Year Experience provides several programs that extend to not only freshman, but to all students. These include family weekend, community service days, the Information and Personal Assistance Center (IPAC), and the Community Advocate Program.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Recently the FYE program was awarded the 2006 NASPA Excellence Gold Award, in the category of &quot;Enrollment Management, Orientation, Parents, First-Year, Other-Year and related&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 2008, Jackson's administration has led an effort to form the CLASS Initiative (&quot;Clustered Learning Advocacy and Support for Students&quot;), which requires all sophomores to <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">live on campus</a> and to live with special &quot;residence cluster deans&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The transition to this program began in early 2010 among some resistance from some fraternities and students who had planned to live off campus.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute_people" title="List of Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute people">List of Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>According to the Rensselaer Alumni Association, there are around 90,000 RPI graduates currently living in the United States, and another 4,378 living abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1995, the Alumni Association created the Rensselaer Alumni Hall of Fame.<sup id="cite_ref-AHOF_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AHOF-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several notable 19th&nbsp;century civil engineers graduated from RPI. These include the visionary of the transcontinental railroad, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Judah" title="Theodore Judah">Theodore Judah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">Brooklyn Bridge</a> engineer <a href="/wiki/Washington_Roebling" title="Washington Roebling">Washington Roebling</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_W._G._Ferris" title="George W. G. Ferris" class="mw-redirect">George W.&nbsp;G. Ferris</a> (who designed and built the original <a href="/wiki/Ferris_Wheel" title="Ferris Wheel">Ferris Wheel</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Leffert_L._Buck" title="Leffert L. Buck">Leffert L. Buck</a>, the chief engineer of the <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg_Bridge" title="Williamsburg Bridge">Williamsburg Bridge</a> in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-AHOF_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AHOF-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many RPI graduates have made important inventions, including <a href="/wiki/Allen_B._DuMont" title="Allen B. DuMont">Allen B. DuMont</a> ('24),<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> creator of the first commercial television; <a href="/wiki/Keith_Millis" title="Keith Millis">Keith D. Millis</a> ('38),<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> inventor of <a href="/wiki/Ductile_iron" title="Ductile iron">ductile iron</a>; <a href="/wiki/Marcian_Hoff" title="Marcian Hoff">Ted Hoff</a> ('58),<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> father of the microprocessor; <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Tomlinson" title="Raymond Tomlinson" class="mw-redirect">Raymond Tomlinson</a> ('63),<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> often credited with the invention of e-mail; inventor of the digital camera <a href="/wiki/Steven_Sasson" title="Steven Sasson">Steven Sasson</a><sup id="cite_ref-The_Rediff_Interview.2FSteven_J_Sasson.2C_inventor_of_the_digital_camera_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Rediff_Interview.2FSteven_J_Sasson.2C_inventor_of_the_digital_camera-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Priem" title="Curtis Priem">Curtis Priem</a> ('82), designer of the first graphics processor for the PC, and co-founder of <a href="/wiki/NVIDIA" title="NVIDIA" class="mw-redirect">NVIDIA</a>.</p> 
     <p>In addition to NVIDIA, RPI graduates have also gone on to found or co-found major companies such as <a href="/wiki/John_Wiley_and_Sons" title="John Wiley and Sons" class="mw-redirect">John Wiley and Sons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Instruments" title="Texas Instruments">Texas Instruments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Semiconductor" title="Fairchild Semiconductor">Fairchild Semiconductor</a>, <a href="/wiki/PSINet" title="PSINet">PSINet</a>, <a href="/wiki/MapInfo" title="MapInfo">MapInfo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adelphia_Communications" title="Adelphia Communications" class="mw-redirect">Adelphia Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Level_3_Communications" title="Level 3 Communications">Level&nbsp;3 Communications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garmin" title="Garmin">Garmin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bugle_Boy" title="Bugle Boy">Bugle Boy</a>. Several RPI graduates have played a part in the <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">U.S. space program</a>: <a href="/wiki/George_Low" title="George Low">George Low</a> (B.Eng. 1948, M.S. 1950) was manager of the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo&nbsp;11 project</a> and served as president of RPI, and astronauts <a href="/wiki/John_Swigert" title="John Swigert" class="mw-redirect">John L. Swigert,&nbsp;Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Mastracchio" title="Richard Mastracchio">Richard Mastracchio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_R._Wiseman" title="Gregory R. Wiseman">Gregory R. Wiseman</a>, and space tourist <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Tito" title="Dennis Tito">Dennis Tito</a> are alumni.</p> 
     <p>Political figures who graduated from RPI included <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_judge" title="United States federal judge">federal judge</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_J._Gajarsa" title="Arthur J. Gajarsa">Arthur J. Gajarsa</a> (B.S. 1962), <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">DARPA</a> director <a href="/wiki/Tony_Tether" title="Tony Tether" class="mw-redirect">Tony Tether</a>, Representative <a href="/wiki/John_Olver" title="John Olver">John Olver</a> of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 1st congressional district">Massachusetts's 1st congressional district</a>, and Senators <a href="/wiki/Mark_Shepard" title="Mark Shepard">Mark Shepard</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_R._Dennis" title="George R. Dennis">George R. Dennis</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable ice hockey players include NHL <a href="/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame" title="Hockey Hall of Fame">Hockey Hall of Famer</a> and 5-time NHL All Star <a href="/wiki/Adam_Oates" title="Adam Oates">Adam Oates</a> (1985), <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> winner and former NHL All Star <a href="/wiki/Mike_McPhee" title="Mike McPhee">Mike McPhee</a> (1982), two-time <a href="/wiki/Calder_Cup" title="Calder Cup">Calder Cup</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Neil_Little" title="Neil Little">Neil Little</a> (1994), former NHL All Rookie <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A9_Juneau" title="Jo&eacute; Juneau">Jo&eacute; Juneau</a> (1991), and former NHL All Star <a href="/wiki/Daren_Puppa" title="Daren Puppa">Daren Puppa</a> (1985).</p> 
     <p>Other notable alumni include 1973 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Giaever" title="Ivar Giaever">Ivar Giaever</a> (Ph.D. 1964);<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> director of Linux International <a href="/wiki/Jon_Hall_(programmer)" title="Jon Hall (programmer)">Jon Hall</a> (M.S. 1977); <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> president <a href="/wiki/Myles_Brand" title="Myles Brand">Myles Brand</a> (B.S. 1964);<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> adult stem cell pioneer <a href="/wiki/James_Fallon" title="James Fallon">James Fallon</a>; director <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Farrelly" title="Bobby Farrelly">Bobby Farrelly</a> (1981),<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> and David Ferrucci, lead researcher on IBM's <a href="/wiki/Watson_(computer)" title="Watson (computer)">Watson</a>/Jeopardy! project.</p>
